<span id="freeTextContainer17119718652518762325"><blockquote>
  <b>⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱*I Hate Insta-Love*⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱</b>
</blockquote><br/><b>
  <u>Second re-read: 17.02.2020</u>
</b><br/>I don't know how I feel about this re-read. I mean, I like the story, the concept, but.. yeah there's the insta-love (that I haven't even tagged yet :O). The insta-love ruins everything. All of the story is pretty much within a week + two days (I think), and that's waaaaay too short for me. I love Dragos, I absolutely do. And Pia isn't a bad character, quite enjoyable, but there's something that do annoy me about - I just can't fig</span>
  <span id="freeText17119718652518762325" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱*I Hate Insta-Love*⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱</b>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <u>Second re-read: 17.02.2020</u>
</b><br>I don't know how I feel about this re-read. I mean, I like the story, the concept, but.. yeah there's the insta-love (that I haven't even tagged yet :O). The insta-love ruins everything. All of the story is pretty much within a week + two days (I think), and that's waaaaay too short for me. I love Dragos, I absolutely do. And Pia isn't a bad character, quite enjoyable, but there's something that do annoy me about - I just can't figure it out. Perhaps it's the way she handled finding out about her <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[pregnancy <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Overall, I skimmed, I must admit to that. I didn't skim at the conversation parts, but the information part? I did. I truly did. I wasn't interested in that. I don't even know why I even started reading this one again.<br><br>I mean, I've changed in my opinions so much that me still liking this book was not something that was written in stone. But I wanted to read about an animalistic, controlling and possessive, alpha male and Dragos is pretty much all that. But the book has a too short timespan and there's something missing in my opinion. I just don't know what that is yet. That being said, the rating being lower and the spamming might have been due to my migraine, and me taking medicine for it that made me quite tried and unable to focus. <b>So I'm not gonna take the star rating down from four stars to three even though I'm lowing the number rating</b>. I feel like I need to re-read the book while I'm "clearheaded" and better to give it a proper rating.<br><br><b><u>The Characters</u>:</b><br>→ <b>Pia Alessandra Giovanni</b> (25), half-human and half-Wyr. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Is a unicorn - a rare breed that was almost hunted to extinction. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>→ <b>Dragos Cuelebre</b> (born along with the solar system, give or take), a dragon and one of the eldest and most powerful of the Wyr. He was universally acknowledged as one of the oldest Powers in the Elder Races and recognized as the iron-fisted ruler of the New York Wyrkind demesne. He was also a major, if shadowy, power player in the Washington political scene.<br>→ <b>Rune Ainissesthai</b>, Drago's first and a gryphon, and of of Dragos' sentinels. All seven of his sentinels were immortal creatures strong in Power. They were also raptors of some sort.<br>→ <b>Quentin Caeravorn</b> (could have been anywhere from 35 to 135), owner of Elfie’s bar (a good neighborhood club with a steady, loyal clientele of mixed breeds from all three races) and Pia's boss (worked there since she was twenty-one). Pia guesses he's part Elven.<br>→ <b>Keith ‘Captain Fantastic’ Hollins</b>, human and ex-boyfriend of Pia. A gambling addict. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Killed by Urien. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>→ <b>Thistle ‘Tricks’ Periwinkle</b>, a faerie and PR director for Cuelebre Enterprises and one of the more famous spokespersons from the Elder Races. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Is Urien's nephew, the rightful hair to the throne of the Dark Fae - Urien had killed her parents. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>→ <b>Urien Lorelle</b>, the Dark Fae King, was one of the seven rulers of the Elder Races; his demesne was seated in the greater Chicago area, and he was the guy Dragos most loved to hate. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Dragos kills him at the end of the book. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>→ <b>Constantine</b>, <b>Graydon</b> and <b>Bayne</b>, gryphons and Dragos' sentinels. Each gryphons is responsible for keeping the peace in one of the four sectors of Dragos' demesne. <br>→ <b>Grym</b>, one of Dragos' sentinels, a gargoyle, was in charge of corporate security for Cuelebre Enterprises.<br>→ <b>Tiago Black</b>, one of Dragos' sentinels. One of the three known thunderbirds in existence, headed Dragos’s private army.<br>→ <b>Aryal</b>, one of Dragos' sentinels. A harpy who was in charge of investigations. She was not known for having a serene temperament. There was a reason she had risen to such preeminence in Dragos' Court. <br>→ <b>Kristoff ‘Kris’</b>, a Wyr-bear and one of four of Dragos' assistants.<br>→ <b>Ferion</b>, a powerful Elf.<br>→ <b>Calondir</b>, The Elven High Lord, and his consort, the lady Beluviel.<br>→ <b>Adela</b>, a witch and owner of the shop Divinus. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Killed. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b><u>Quick basic facts</u>:</b><br><b>Genre</b>: - (Adult) Paranormal Romance (M/F).<br><b>Series</b>: - Series, Book One.<br><b>Love triangle?</b> - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>Cheating?</b> - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>HEA?</b> - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Yes. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>Favorite character?</b> - Dragos Cuelebre.<br><b>Would I read more by this author/or of series?</b> - Some of them.<br><b>Would I recommend this book/series?</b> -Sure, Dragos is hot.<br><b>Will I read this again in the future?</b> - Unsure.<br><b>New Rating</b> - 3.5/3 stars.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445268775i/16623124.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <u>Re-read: 05.10.15</u>
</b><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> "Sounds a lot love love to me.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444333552i/16485173._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I am cursed with a terminal case of curiosity," he said. "I am jealous, selfish, acquisitive, territorial and possessive. I have a terrible temper, and I know I can be a cruel son of a bitch." He cocked his head. "I used to eat people, you know.” </i>

One corner of his mouth twitched. He gave himself a deep shock when he burst into an explosive guffaw. <br><br>She's dammed if she does and dammed if she isn't. Although Pia is a Wyr, she is a half blood. Never feeling as if she has ever fit in anywhere she has always had to leave at a moment’s notice. Don’t get attached to people, places or things. She makes one small error and it all blows up in her face. <br><br>Dragos one of the most powerful Wyr’s has had a thief take something from him. He is a dragon and dragon’s hoard. <br><br>Dragos doesn't like that something he owns has been taken from him doesn't matter that it is a penny. But he finds that there is something different about this particular scent. He is curious how to get a hold of the little thief and a cherry Coke with twizzlers. <br><br>I adore Pia. She has had to steal, she is on the run, she gets kidnapped on top of that the Dark Fae King is very interested in her and destroying Dragos as Dragos has something he really wants. <br><br>What I didn't expect is what kind of Wyr Pia is.   <span id="freeText16253889798109565515" style="display:none"><b>OH WOW!!! Never in my wildest dreams would I have thought this book would be this good! I absolutely adored it!</b> Helloooooo new favorite! I'm totally hooked, and I can't wait to see more books released in the series.<br /><br /><b>What's not to love about a Dragon shifter? ...</b><br />Dragos Cuelebre = HAWT! You just don't have any idea how hot this guy was. Seriously, my fav in a while, I loved everything about him. The guy was totally alpha material, a caveman on the loose, LOL. He was all you're mine and there's no discussion about it. <br /><blockquote>"I am cursed with a terminal case of curiosity," he said. "I am jealous, selfish, acquisitive, territorial and possessive. I have a terrible temper, and I know I can be a cruel son of a bitch." He cocked his head. "I used to eat people, you know."</blockquote><br />He made me laugh out loud so many times with his attitude, and it's not that he was annoying for being so MACHO because he constantly realized he was doing something wrong and tried to change it to make the heroine feel better. He just couldn't help being like that because the guy is 11000 years old,lol, let's just give him a break. What I loved the most was to see him comprehending what love was because of the new feelings the heroine awoke in him.<br /><blockquote>"He kissed the palm of her hand. "It means, you stupid woman, that I am learning too. Now you listen to me. I never stop thinking about you. You're with me everywhere I go but I miss you when we're apart. I've already shown that I will kill for you. I would also die for you. You make me laugh. You make me happy. You're my miracle and my home...I will always come for you, always want you, and always need you. We clear?" <br /><br />She had begun to glow. "Sounds a lot like love to me." </blockquote><br />You see? sweet and sexy. But he was so much more than an amazing personality ... he was a dragon, a being who was alive through the beginnings and ending of empires, who saw all the changes the world went through, someone you could talk to all your life and never get bored. And dude ---&gt; A DRAGON, I don't know why but for some reason I just find that totally hot.<br /><br /><b>A very peculiar heroine ...</b><br />I usually never like heroines or remember them much, but I loved this one. I liked that while she preferred not to fight she was able to kick everybody's asses if she wanted to. I loved that through out all the story we knew there was a mystery around her but not exactly what. She had an amazing sense of humor and personality, some of the best jokes were from her. I really liked her.<br /><blockquote>"He stared at her neck. Realization pulsed. He was looking at the bite he had given her. A hard length was growing against her hip. “So, is that your long, scaly, reptilian tail, or are you just happy to see me?” No, she did not just say that. Did she?" </blockquote><br /><br /><b>Then there was the most mind-blowing plot and world building you have ever seen ...</b><br />A Dragon king and his most trusted sentinels, the Gryphons. 2 different Fey Courts, Elves and other Elder races as some other minor races. So much power and magic, what's not to love about this series? The characters were amazing and I just can't wait to read more!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16253889798109565515" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17718571778260792051"><blockquote>I’m sorry, <i>the message said.<br/>The theft was a violation of privacy. It was an unbelievable act of impudence and disrespect. Not only that, it was—baffling. He was murderous,</i> incandescent <i>with fury. He was older than sin and could not remember when he had last been in such a rage.<br/>He looked at the paper again.</i><br/>I’m sorry I had to take your penny. Here’s another to replace it.<br/><i>Yep, that’s what it said.<br/>One corner of his mouth twitched. He gave himself a deep shock when he burst into an explosive guffaw.</i></blockquote><br/><br/>A</span>
  <span id="freeText17718571778260792051" style="display:none"><blockquote>I’m sorry, <i>the message said.<br />The theft was a violation of privacy. It was an unbelievable act of impudence and disrespect. Not only that, it was—baffling. He was murderous,</i> incandescent <i>with fury. He was older than sin and could not remember when he had last been in such a rage.<br />He looked at the paper again.</i><br />I’m sorry I had to take your penny. Here’s another to replace it.<br /><i>Yep, that’s what it said.<br />One corner of his mouth twitched. He gave himself a deep shock when he burst into an explosive guffaw.</i></blockquote><br /><br />And this is how the story begins. Pia, a half-breed, is blackmailed by her ex-boyfriend into stealing something from the dragon's vault.She does just that, attracting the attention of the one and only dragon on earth, Dragos. He is extremely old (as old as the Solar System) and bored. Pia is just the thing to bring him back to life and give him something entertaining. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>He stared at her neck. Realization pulsed. He was looking at the bite he had given her. A hard length was growing against her hip. “So, is that your long, scaly, reptilian tail, or are you just happy to see me?” No, she did not just say that. Did she?</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />They are funny together and one does not really realize the insta-lust until it is too late. If my calculations are correct they have sex (the real thing, not the dream sex) two or three days after they meet. And of course Pia is a special snowflake and Dragos mates with her. *eye roll* Her Wyr half is actually that of a mythical creature that even the dragon thought to be a legend. Special snowflake, told you!<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"I think you’re my hero," she said. Only half-kidding.<br />He stared at her, the picture of incredulity. "Most people," he said, "think I am a very bad man."<br />She studied his eyes to try to find out if that bothered him. He didn’t seem bothered by them. He seemed discomfited by her. "Well," she said at last, "maybe you’re a very good dragon."</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />On the other hand, I have to appreciate the lack of love triangles. The story is just about the two of them and neither acts in that stupid YA let's-make-him/her-jealous way. Thank the Universe for small favours, right?<br /><br />So this is not the worst PNR book out there, but not the best either. *shrugs*</span>

My only issue were the rapid mood swings between the H/h toward the end. While they were understandable, it was jarring in places. I look forward to reading the next in this series. Highly recommend to </span>

<div id="review_139981968" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Mandi Schreiner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2704703-mandi-schreiner"><img alt="Mandi Schreiner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368979996p2/2704703.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mandi Schreiner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mandi Schreiner" href="/user/show/2704703-mandi-schreiner">Mandi Schreiner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139981968" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7026120548348760687">Favorite Quote: “There’s my bad boy,” she whispered. God, he was breathtaking.<br/><br/>I read a lot of books. I read a lot of paranormal books. So when one comes into the Smexy household that is exciting, refreshing and just all around awesome, it is cause for celebration!<br/><br/>Dragon Bound by Thea Harrison is the first book in the Elder Races series. Our hero, Dragos Cuelebre is of the Wyr, a group of powerful, ancient shapeshifters. Dragos more specifically is a rare dragon-shifter created around the time of</span>
  <span id="freeText7026120548348760687" style="display:none">Favorite Quote: “There’s my bad boy,” she whispered. God, he was breathtaking.<br /><br />I read a lot of books. I read a lot of paranormal books. So when one comes into the Smexy household that is exciting, refreshing and just all around awesome, it is cause for celebration!<br /><br />Dragon Bound by Thea Harrison is the first book in the Elder Races series. Our hero, Dragos Cuelebre is of the Wyr, a group of powerful, ancient shapeshifters. Dragos more specifically is a rare dragon-shifter created around the time of the solar system – so yes, he is ancient to say the least. In present day he is head of the Wyr demesnes located in New York city. The other six demesnes, including Elven, Fae etc…reside in other parts of the United States. He is extremely powerful, wealthy and demands loyalty and obedience from everyone in his control. So when someone breaks into his hoard, something that has never happened before and steals from him, his anger as he takes to the sky in his dragon form can literally be felt and heard from everyone in the city.<br /><br />Pia Giovanni is a half-breed – half human, half wyr. Raised by her mother who embedded in her mind to never tell anyone what her half-wyr side is, she has always been on the run. But now she has herself in a bit of a bind. She let her guard down with her ex-boyfriend Keith and revealed to him a bit about herself. Something she has never done with another before. Then Keith turned out to be a jerk and to cover his gambling debts, is now blackmailing her with this secret information about herself. He hands over to her a finding charm which with her special powers leads her directly into Dragos’ hoard and demands that she steal something from Dragos to appease his “associates.” She gets in and steals one of his pennies.<br /><br />When Dragos discovers this theft, he makes it his mission to find who did this. But soon, they both realize there is a bigger player at stake. The Dark Fae King and Dragos have bad blood and a war is on the horizon.<br /><br />When we first meet Dragos, he reminded me very much of Raphael from Nalini Singh’s Guild Hunter series. He is extremely powerful, intense, dark and just a bad ass. But Dragos soon comes into his own. He has been around since the beginning of time, yet some modern things still confuse him. Like slurpees and twizzlers. But don’t let that trick you because he runs one of the biggest corporations in the world. Cuelebre Towers employees thousands of people and he rules with a strict hand. But his dragon side also rules his actions throughout this book - something Pia must come to terms with:<br /><br />Something very light tickled her forearms that covered the back of her head. It whuffled in her hair.<br /><br />She scratched an arm. “Did you kill the Fae horses?”<br /><br />The whuffling stopped. Dragos said in a cautious voice, “Was I not supposed to?”<br /><br />She shrugged. “It just wasn’t their fault.”<br /><br />“If it helps any, I was hungry and ate one.” Another whuffle.<br /><br />When Dragos finally tracks down Pia, his anger soon turns to fascination. He quickly discovers her sticky situation with being blackmailed and realizes a bigger player is calling the shots. He finds himself no longer bored, and very physically attracted to this half breed.<br /><br />Pia is a really great heroine. Strong, outspoken, and stands up to the over-bearing Dragos. He is kind of a “caveman” when it comes to romance. He isn’t suave, or charming. He expects her to follow his orders when it comes to her safety but also in the romance department. But as Pia comes to mean more to him, he wants to learn to be a better lover. I love how we are constantly reminded of how powerful and old he really is:<br /><br />“You are never to do that again,” he said between his teeth. “Do you understand?”<br /><br />“Dragos,” she said, speaking with care because he was still so upset. “You’ve got to stop giving me orders.”<br /><br />No matter how gently she said it, it was still like a spark to dry tinder.<br /><br />“Fuck you,” he snapped. He thrust his face down to hers, eyes flaring to lava and features hardening. “You’re mine. And you. Can’t. Leave.”<br /><br />“Whoa, there. I don’t know what to say to you. You’re like some stalker guy on steroids.” She threw back her hands and rolled her eyes. “You are aware, aren’t you, that you can’t have slaves any longer. You know, abolition. Big war. Happened a hundred and forty, forty-five years ago.”<br /><br />“Human history, human terms,” he snarled. “They mean nothing to me.”<br /><br />Pia is strong-willed and butts heads with him about this behavior on many occasions. But there is also humor and warmth in their relationship. Their romance is a quick one in this book – I believe the entire book takes place over about five days. Which I know seems crazy, but it is totally believable. Dragos has the “mine” concept from very early on, and Pia herself desperate not to be lonely in life, falls for him just as quickly.<br /><br />The romance is very erotic, and just as intense as Dragos himself. I also adored the supporting characters. Rune, Dragos’ “First” and best friend along with Dragos’ other trusted friends guard Pia with their life, although they don’t like her at first. But Dragos soon puts them in their place:<br /><br />“Thief or not, she is mine and I’m keeping her. If a single hair on that young woman’s head is harmed, you four bastards better be slaughtered and in pieces when I find you.”<br /><br />Oh yes, Dragos is that much of a bad ass.<br /><br /> The writing is just superb. There are a few scenes where the action is violent and rough that just made my hair stand on end. Chapter seven holds my absolute favorite scene in the book. Dragos and Pia have been captured and Dragos knows he can’t immediately get them out of harms way. For such a powerful, irate being having to tell this woman who he has started to have protective feelings for that she is going to get hurt, was really amazing to read. You can feel the fear coming off Pia. A brief moment from this chapter:<br /><br />“Here’s what I think is going to happen. They’re going to separate us. They might hurt you.” His grip tightened to the point of pain. “They won’t kill you. They’ll have seen I was tending to you in some way, so they’ll want to use you as leverage to control me. Goblins have no interest in human women. They’ won’t rape you.”<br /><br />A spasm of trembling hit her, and then it was gone again and she was calm. “It’s all right,” she told him. “I’m all right. I’m glad you’re telling me this.”<br /><br />“That’s my good brave girl.”<br /><br />What follows is a terribly violent, emotionally filled chapter that just blew me away.<br /><br />This world is really fantastic – exciting, very sexy and humorous. Fans of paranormal romance must read this book.<br /><br />Rating: A</span>
  <a data-text-id="7026120548348760687" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_166068339" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/166068339" />
    <a title="Anzu The Great Destroyer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer"><img alt="Anzu The Great Destroyer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455829739p2/2278800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/166068339?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anzu The Great Destroyer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anzu The Great Destroyer" href="/user/show/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer">Anzu The Great Destroyer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11141590-dragon-bound">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">hopeless romantics</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Anzu by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4290492-aly-is-so-frigging-bored">Aly is so frigging bored</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=fat-kitty-judges-you">fat-kitty-judges-you</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=big-fucking-nope">big-fucking-nope</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=reviewed-2011">reviewed-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=cheesetacular">cheesetacular</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=is-it-just-me-goddammit">is-it-just-me-goddammit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=welcome-to-snoozeville">welcome-to-snoozeville</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=dafuq-did-i-just-read">dafuq-did-i-just-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=whiny-bitches">whiny-bitches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=furry-wild-and-rabid">furry-wild-and-rabid</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2278800-anzu-the-great-destroyer?shelf=wtf-am-i-doing">wtf-am-i-doing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer166068339" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8757398649394366045">I really was attracted by the story when I saw this book so said I gots to read it! Plus some of my friends rated it well so I said what the hell.<br/><br/>Now please don’t kill me or anything but I didn’t like it so much. I’ll even tell you why later on. I have good reasons and hopefully you won’t beat me up.. too much. <br/><br/>Ok so we have a dragon who’s older than dirt, a selfish little (or not) bastard who loved to collect shiny things. Then this girl comes and steals a penny. She replaces the penny but stil</span>
  <span id="freeText8757398649394366045" style="display:none">I really was attracted by the story when I saw this book so said I gots to read it! Plus some of my friends rated it well so I said what the hell.<br><br>Now please don’t kill me or anything but I didn’t like it so much. I’ll even tell you why later on. I have good reasons and hopefully you won’t beat me up.. too much. <br><br>Ok so we have a dragon who’s older than dirt, a selfish little (or not) bastard who loved to collect shiny things. Then this girl comes and steals a penny. She replaces the penny but still! She stole it! Dun dun duuun *dramatic music* Killing starts in…. three….. two… one…… I expected something bloodier; revenge, verbal assault, maybe some spanking. But unfortunately he turned all mushy on her and nothing happened. And there’s my problem. I’ll get back to that later. <br><br>Now I have some questions. What is a penny to a filthy rich dragon? I get it, he minded the whole stealing and crap part but still. She took a freakin’ penny! She could have taken his dirty socks or something if they needed a tracking spell. How did she know it was a rare penny? What if it was just a regular one that he would use to buy his daily ice-cream. Now I get why he was so angry. Whoever touches my ice-cream money dies!! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380349448i/703446.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Thea Harrison created a pretty decent universe in this book. We have lots of magical creatures running around doing their thing. Different realms where you can travel and have tea parties. Elf bread that makes an orgasm look like a walkabout surrounded by old people. You know? Crazy stuff. My problem was her passiveness towards all these cool elements. She could have done a wonderful job creating an action-filled story. She could have played with our emotions, make us love some characters, hate others. But unfortunately it didn’t work for me. Maybe it did for you, and if so cheers!, but on this side of the planet… nopes. <br><br>Another shortcoming came from the characters. They were too rigid. Their dialogue is too stiff and their reactions are the same. They’re too groomed, too shiny. Too much talk and little action gets boring after a while. <br><br>My biggest problem was Pia and Dragos’… relationship? The easiest turn of events evar? I mean the woman stole from the big bad dragon, which scares the shit out of everyone. What’s the logical reaction here? Ass kicking! Torture! Pillow fights! What happened in the book? The dude saw her got a huge boner and wanted to add her to his collection of treasures and whatnot. Ok you can say this could actually work. But now we go to Pia’s (the thief) camp. What did she do? She was übercalm and just accepted everything. <br><br>I actually loved his reaction towards her but it got me thinking why is he so possessive? Is it because he sees her as an object? A toy? A gem? He doesn’t want any other boys playing with his toys? I doubt it’s love since it’s too early. Lust? Maybe ‘cause they’re two horny bastards. But still this reaction is too much. Love at first sight… or lust at first sight as our case is. This combined with seeing her as an object. Way to go! <br><br>Pia is too much of a damsel in distress for my taste. I like fighters that put a bit of trouble in their relationships. And this must go both ways. I feel like their – whatever this is, flirt, fling, relationship – is just too <b>easy</b>. I have to put this in bold. The whole world’s on Dragos’ shoulders and he just carries it with a smile on his face. He’s actually the only one who puts a bit of action in the book. Pia is too passive and silly. She’s not heroine material, at least for me she’s not. She is a big part of the reason why I didn’t like the book so much. <br><br>Ok so Pia’s a vegetarian. I really wanna pick on this. It’s not like I have a problem with vegetarians but I know a joke or whatever this is so have to comment about it. What do carnivores say to vegetarians? Our food sh*ts on your food. And what do vegetarians say to carnivores? Your food eats ours with the sh*t on it. Loool it makes me have second thoughts about what I should be eating. <br><br>Another thought on Dragos. Shouldn’t a creature like him, once he lived for so many years, take an interest in studying? Imagine studying almost everything, you name it, math, physics, chemistry, etc for so many years. You end up being supersmart, then your brain swells up like Megamind and you rule the world. Why did he turn up just a businessman? Does he know Obama? Does he play golf with Putin? I think he does… Putin is his wingman…<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380349448i/703447.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Another big problem that I had was related to Dragos. The guy doesn’t seem like a - uhm how to put this? – guy (duh) in some scenes. Especially in dialogues. I feel like Pia is having a conversation with herself rather than a dangerous dragon. Badasses don’t talk like that. They’re too tough for this even when they’re in love – or whatever the hell Dragos is feeling for her. I was constantly screaming at my Kindle – GROW SOME BALLS!!! <br><br>Towards the mid-end or something Pia ended up locked inside the dragon’s house (aka nest). I saw this similar to a bird getting locked in a cage. A possession he’d visit from time to time, screw and then leave to get on with his business or whatever the hell he does. Beats the crap out of a blowup doll. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380349448i/703448.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And my problem with all this is how calm she is! Too damn calm!!! Woman get angry and beat him up!! I guess she’s happy with being a kept woman. And in the end this whole situation didn’t get settled. I didn’t get my answer of how she’ll live with Dragos, if she’ll have a job or something. I’m not a feminist but some things are exaggerated. This is one of them. <br><br>Spoiler alert! I must pick on this so beware all you spidermonkeys! <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I had a feeling that Pia will get pregnant. It was so damn predictable and, sorry to say it, lame. I don’t know why but stories with pregnancies turn me off. They bore me and I simply don’t like them. Too much drama where you could have had a nice story. <br><br>Another problem of mine: the unicorn deal. I mean seriously?!?! She’s a f*cking unicorn?!? I’m sorry but that’s kinda gay… I was hoping something a bit bloodier. I mean she’s mating with a damn dragon… a dragon and an unicorn is too much for my brain to handle. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Now as a conclusion…. If Thea Harrison improves her characters, focuses a bit more on the beauty of the environment she created and works out some hot ass action then this series will become great. Hell maybe even amazing. So if you’re looking for an action-packed gig this is not the book for you. If you like sweet love stories then give it a try. You’ll surely like it. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380349448i/703449.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Top 5 quotes</b><br><br><b>#5</b><i> "I will not put you in harm’s way.” He kept her head cradled in one hand and put an arm around her. He murmured, “I do not endanger my treasures.”</i><br><br><b>#4</b><i> He turned his face, found her mouth and kissed her as he held them so tight together at pelvis and hip, for a while it felt as if they had fused together and become one creature, light and dark, yin and yang.</i><br><br><b>#3</b><i> “So, is that your long, scaly, reptilian tail, or are you just happy to see me?”<br>No, she did not just say that.</i><br><br><b>#2</b><i> "Hey, what if they stopped throwing a fit at you walking across their backyard. It’s not like you ate their tulips or dug holes in their lawn. You didn’t piss on any trees when I wasn’t looking, did you?”</i><br><br><b>#1</b><i> “I am cursed with a terminal case of curiosity,” he said. “I am jealous, selfish, acquisitive, territorial and possessive. I have a terrible temper, and I know I can be a cruel son of a bitch.” He cocked his head. “I used to eat people, you know.”</i><br><br>Read the review on <a href="http://zombiehazard.blogspot.com/2011/06/dragon-bound-elder-races-1.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"></a>ZombieHazard.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer168488138" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2666886272905098279">4.5 stars<br/><br/>I can't help it. The entire time I was reading this a huge part of me felt like a traitor to The Cause. <i>Domineering men are not sexy!</i> Isn't that what we're supposed to teach our daughters? <br/>And yet...<i>my daughter wasn't reading this, was she</i>? <br/>No. <i>I</i> was. <b>And it was hot</b>! <br/>Perhaps we should amend The Rules, and say that domineering men are <i>only</i> sexy in fantasy novels? Yes. I think that will do quite nicely. <br/><i>
  <b>Pssst</b>
</i><br/>But in all seriousness, marry the guy who helps you out with the laundry!<br/> <i>Mmm</i></span>
  <span id="freeText2666886272905098279" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br /><br />I can't help it. The entire time I was reading this a huge part of me felt like a traitor to The Cause. <i>Domineering men are not sexy!</i> Isn't that what we're supposed to teach our daughters? <br />And yet...<i>my daughter wasn't reading this, was she</i>? <br />No. <i>I</i> was. <b>And it was hot</b>! <br />Perhaps we should amend The Rules, and say that domineering men are <i>only</i> sexy in fantasy novels? Yes. I think that will do quite nicely. <br /><i>
  <b>Pssst</b>
</i><br />But in all seriousness, marry the guy who helps you out with the laundry!<br /> <i>Mmmmmm. Look at him separate the lights from the darks...Growr!</i><br />What? Trust me, girls....one day the sight of a man with a mop in one hand, and a bucket of Pine Sol in the other will be the sexiest thing you've <i>ever</i> seen.<br /><br />Ok, too many people have already done a great job reviewing the story, so I won't bore you with my version of the details. However, I will list the top three things I loved about the book.<br /><br /><b>1.</b> The fun and witty banter between Pia and Dragos<br /><b>2.</b> The smokin' hot lurve scenes<br /><b>3.</b> The fact that you don't find out <i>what</i> Pia is until the book is almost over.<br /><br />This is such a fun fantasy/romance novel that I would recommend it wholeheartedly to anyone with any interest in this genre!<br /><br /><i>On a side note, the dude on the cover <b>could not</b> look any goofier. First, he's too skinny to match the physical description of the main character. I could snap that kid like a twig!<br />Second, that purple gargoyle-thing looks like it's shooting out of the side of his poor malnourished shoulder, and for some reason that really bothered me.<br />Not that any of that has any bearing on the book...</i></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer162938353" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11063425517802100577">I made a mistake before reading this book and I wish I wouldn’t have. Usually when I <i>know</i> that I’ll be reading a book soon, I stay far away from reviews and conversations about the book. It’s not that I’m afraid I’ll be spoiled, it’s just that I don’t want to go into a book looking for a positive or a negative that someone else had. Often I’ll find myself focusing on things that I never would have noticed on my own, and I hate that. I want to go in blind and see what my raw reaction is. <br/><br/>Since I </span>
  <span id="freeText11063425517802100577" style="display:none">I made a mistake before reading this book and I wish I wouldn’t have. Usually when I <i>know</i> that I’ll be reading a book soon, I stay far away from reviews and conversations about the book. It’s not that I’m afraid I’ll be spoiled, it’s just that I don’t want to go into a book looking for a positive or a negative that someone else had. Often I’ll find myself focusing on things that I never would have noticed on my own, and I hate that. I want to go in blind and see what my raw reaction is. <br /><br />Since I know this about myself, I rarely break this unwritten rule. But almost all of my Goodreads friends were reading this book! It seemed to be everywhere I looked on blogs and the status updates on Goodreads were too tempting to resist! So…I admit it, I cracked. I read all those updates and all of the resulting conversations. And my expectations started ramping up. I heard Dragos compared time and time again to Raphael from the <b>Guild Hunter</b> series by <b>Nalini Singh</b>. If it had been one or two people, I probably would have ignored it, but there were a lot of them saying that. <br /><br />It’s not that Dragos was a bad hero, it’s just that I was expecting something else when I heard him likened to Raphael. I expected him to be dark, intense, and kind of scary. Even though I liked him, I felt like I was always waiting for that intensity. I just wish I hadn’t gone in expecting something else. The book suffered because I spent so much time looking for something that it lacked. Don’t be like me, people. Don’t let your expectations get the best of you.<br /><br />Despite not seeing intensity in Dragos, I did see a lot to like. I loved how the author wrote him with such an animalistic personality. His behavior didn’t always fit with acceptable human behavior, but Pia took the differences in him well. His refusal to tell anyone—even his men—too much information about Pia was an example of the little quirks that made him seem dragon-like. He was secretive, jealously protective of what he considered “his”, and could be cold when the situation warranted it. I probably would have found the split second mood swings irritating in another man, but it didn’t bother me with Dragos. It just served as a nice example of how alien his thinking and behavior could be.<br /><br />I was very hesitant about Pia in the beginning. I think I was supposed to sympathize with her, but I found her kind of whiny and irritating. The more I read about her, the more I liked her, but I continued to have problems with her throughout the book and never quite loved her the way most did. <br /><br /> I found it irritating that her behavior and personality seemed to vary throughout the book. She was strong and mouthy one minute, and overwhelmed and giving up the next. I didn’t need to her to be a badass, but I needed some consistency. She was incredibly impressive in a scene involving the goblins—I <i>loved</i> that whole interlude—but then she turned around and gave up <i>after they were free</i>. It was so frustrating! And did anyone else notice how often she slept and left Dragos to handle the situation in times of crisis? <br /><br />Although I had issues with the characters, I liked Pia and Dragos together. They meshed well and they were refreshingly straightforward about their attraction to each other. It seemed a little abrupt in the beginning, but I just shrugged and went with it. Their playfulness and joking made their interactions fun and the chemistry between them was great. I laughed when Pia tried to teach Dragos manners and loved watching Dragos try to accustom himself to caring about her and wanting to please her.<br /><br />I really liked the side characters and was pleased that they were more than just sequel bait. They were a lot of fun—especially the next book’s heroine, Tricks—and I loved that they were different from the shifters normally seen in PNR. Dragos’s team had gryphons, a gargoyle, thunderbirds (awesome!), and even a harpy. I’m really curious to get to see a thunderbird in the next book because I've never read about one before. I thought they all became BFF’s with the heroine a little too easily, but that’s not exactly unique to this book. I frequently find myself with that complaint in PNR.<br /><br />I was very impressed with the author for choosing such unique paranormal species. I spent the whole book trying to figure out what Pia was and why her mom was so worried about her keeping it a secret. I had a few guesses, but I never came close. Kudos to the author for trying something so different! <br /><br />There was a surprise development between Pia and Dragos that cropped up very close to the end. I did not like the fact that it was included at all. It almost dropped my grade to a 3 ½, but I enjoyed the rest of the book enough to not let it get to me that much. I just thought it was unnecessary and I had no sympathy for Pia’s irrational behavior. <br /><br />Although I didn’t love it as much as most, and found the overall tone more light and funny than intense, I still thought it was a fun new PNR. I’m really looking forward to trying out the next book because Tricks was hilarious in this one. If you’re on the fence about this one, I say try it out. Besides, it has dragons! That’s so infrequent that I snatch them up whenever I hear about them.<br /><br /><b>Favorite Quote:</b> <br /><blockquote>
  <p>He dug his fingers into her hair and lifted up the strands. "I want some of your hair."</p>
  <p>She lifted her head. "What?"</p>
  <p>"I said I want some of your hair. Give me a lock and I'll forgive you for breaking and entering."</p>
  <p>"Oh-kay. Sure." She squinted at him. "So I give you a lock of my hair, take you to the Elven border and drop you off?"</p>
  <p>He laughed. "I never said I was letting you go. I just said I'll forgive you."</p>
  <p>"I knew that had to be too easy," she muttered. "You're just not a straight road, are you?"</p>
</blockquote><br />Review originally posted on <a href="http://www.fictionvixen.com/2011/05/review-dragon-bound-by-thea-harrison.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Fiction Vixen</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11063425517802100577" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_205430494" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/205430494" />
    <a title="Catie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1886642-catie"><img alt="Catie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385169623p2/1886642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/205430494?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catie" href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Catie by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer205430494" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3947085347864720051">Well, this is a nice diverting piece of fluff, which is just what I needed to kick off this week. The first week of school: that magical time when adult Catie, after spending an entire summer in hiding to make way for playgrounds, camps, and story time, gets to come out of hibernation. This book’s main appeal for me was the surprisingly well developed fantasy world. While it’s obvious that the author has borrowed a bit from Tolkien and <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Peter S. Beagle <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, the mythical</span>
  <span id="freeText3947085347864720051" style="display:none">Well, this is a nice diverting piece of fluff, which is just what I needed to kick off this week. The first week of school: that magical time when adult Catie, after spending an entire summer in hiding to make way for playgrounds, camps, and story time, gets to come out of hibernation. This book’s main appeal for me was the surprisingly well developed fantasy world. While it’s obvious that the author has borrowed a bit from Tolkien and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Peter S. Beagle <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, the mythical beasts and the setting feel alive and vivid. For a fantasy buff like me, this is a nice bit of escapism. However, the romance is nothing new.<br /><br />Pia Giovanni has just committed a crime which will change her life forever. Driven by the blackmail of her bastard ex-boyfriend, she has stolen an item from the horde of the powerful Dragos. Sure, all she took was a penny…and she even left a note of apology. But the Dragon Lord is not known for forgiveness or mercy, and it’s only a matter of time before he tracks her down. However, Pia has a lifetime of experience running and hiding. She might have a few tricks up her sleeve that Dragos is not expecting.<br /><br />If you’ve read any number of these books (which I may or may not have done) then you’ll recognize these characters right away. Dragos is the <i>exact same</i> hero character that appears in just about every PNR or even UF that I’ve read. He’s a wealthy, expensive car loving alpha male with an eight pack (because a six pack is sooo passé) and a gooey center of barely caged violence, jealousy, and possessiveness. Harrison takes an interesting turn by incorporating some dragon lore here (for example, his love of shiny pretty things and his need to stash hordes all over the city) but all the hallmarks are still there, and I still just don’t enjoy reading about this man and the relationship dynamics that go along with him.<br /><br />Pia is the willowy, blonde, graceful slip of a thing (who, okay, has some hidden strength…but hates to use it) who ends up getting kidnapped, separated from her friends and family, provided with luxury, and fucked senseless every once in a while (whenever Dragos isn’t off doing his important man-work). There’s plenty of rapey lovin’ and domination (which of course she loves!). And <i>of course</i>, this pair is like night and day, light and dark, which used to refer to something a lot more nuanced and exciting than just their appearances and superficial characteristics. It’s like the classic paradigm of the odd couple has been exaggerated and stretched to the point of silliness. <i> He’s a violent beast who used to eat…PEOPLE!...and she’s a…vegetarian! No, a VEGAN! It’s priceless!</i> Argh.<br /><br />And <i>of course</i> there’s a whole stable of attractive men and women just waiting in the wings to stand in as the main players for future books. The future stars might vary in looks – the light one, the dark one, the short one, the curvy one, perhaps the token intellectual thrown in – but I doubt that the relationship dynamic will change very much. It’s like having a set of dolls that you can take out and play with one pair at a time, except their pelvises aren’t just blank plastic so it’s more fun.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>Exxhhhaaaaalllleee.</b>
</i><br /><br />Okay, time to fess up.<br /><br />Yeah, I’d say about 20% of my blood supply was dedicated to having these concerned, offended thoughts. But the other 80%? Was off having a party. Because this book is kind of sort of incredibly hot. I blame the hibernation.<br /><br /><u>Perfect Musical Pairing</u><br /><br />D’Angelo – <a href="http://www.dailymotion.com/video/xcvzz_d-angelo-untitled-how-does-it-feel_news" rel="nofollow noopener">How Does it Feel?</a><br /><br />I had to go outside of the youtube-verse because it was absolutely imperative that I provide you all with this video. I challenge you to pay any attention at all to the lyrics or the melody or indeed anything at all after about thirty seconds.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3947085347864720051" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer999430132" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2861652607863223682"><br/> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429041944i/14520847._SY540_.jpg' width='540' height='594' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>God forbid I say something wrong witht this review.<br/><br/>Alright. Part 1 of my threeway review (because it's always fun when it's a threeway..)<br/><br/><b>The technicalities</b>:This book was my first Paranormal Romance read and I'm still thanking the Lord above that I saw this book here in GR. Thea Harrison knows how to build a world so perfect that you just can't help wanting to live there.<br/><br/>The plot was the first thing that catched my attention. We have a gutsy albeit unwilling thief. One angry dragon. And a love s</span>
  <span id="freeText2861652607863223682" style="display:none"><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429041944i/14520847._SY540_.jpg" width="540" height="594" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>God forbid I say something wrong witht this review.<br><br>Alright. Part 1 of my threeway review (because it's always fun when it's a threeway..)<br><br><b>The technicalities</b>:This book was my first Paranormal Romance read and I'm still thanking the Lord above that I saw this book here in GR. Thea Harrison knows how to build a world so perfect that you just can't help wanting to live there.<br><br>The plot was the first thing that catched my attention. We have a gutsy albeit unwilling thief. One angry dragon. And a love story that is soo much better than Bella and Edward. I'm usually not a paranormal kind of gal and usually, when we hear the word <b>"paranormal"</b>, we think of werewolves and vampires whatevah. Which is okay if you're the type of person who likes donating blood to the needy. But <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4443809.Thea_Harrison" title="Thea Harrison" rel="nofollow noopener">Thea Harrison</a> introduced me to a paranormal world where there are sexy alphas of all alphas heroes.<br><br>When you look at all the reviews of Dragon Bound, most gave this book a five-star and it was fucking worth it. The author's way of writing is easy to read and you don't have to wrack your head to figure out what the hell is she talking (or writing) about.There are just some authors who tried to twist and use fancy words to make their story more appealing which is wrong. If you want to tell a story, make sure that the readers get what you are saying and I've got to say, Miss Harisson sure knows how to tell a story.<br><br><b>The Characters</b><br><br><b> Dragos Cuelebre</b><br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429128902i/14534385.png" width="540" height="270" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Megahd. I can't reveal much of Dragos charm and dash <i> *snort*</i> without giving much spoiler but honestly guys. If that little pic above is not enough to pique your interest to our Alpha of all Alpha hero, then you're a nut.Nutty nutty nut.<br><br>One thing about Dragos though, he may be an Alpha bad ass motherfucker dragon, but he's never an asshole to Pia.<br><br>****TBC<br></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sXCt9UFYTM5PITSIMsrke5blZcax+G9H5cH1psw/2FuqGlx3I7w2ifHre7CBlFp/vsPslRl0jr4k0S4nJB0Exw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1jVomdR8jWTPXA67LzlPynOQsuuFIflgM/Qgpc6dpk/NX5kbtpj3I3GWQYOcZ/HOW7Y7uC2tGJny5PskJr960w==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer10316078032917049198">I write paranormal romance, urban fantasy, and other stuff. I taught myself to read when I was four. That was around the time I tried to ride my tricycle to work. I wasn't sure where work was, but I knew it had to be interesting if people went there every day. Now I combine my love of books with work, and I don't have to ride my tricycle to get there. My Elder Races series began May, 2011. You can</span>
  <span id="freeText10316078032917049198" style="display:none">I write paranormal romance, urban fantasy, and other stuff. I taught myself to read when I was four. That was around the time I tried to ride my tricycle to work. I wasn't sure where work was, but I knew it had to be interesting if people went there every day. Now I combine my love of books with work, and I don't have to ride my tricycle to get there. My Elder Races series began May, 2011. You can also find me on Twitter and Facebook!</span>
